text:
Definitely a hit... and I thought the leftovers tasted even better!  However, I substituted the mozz and parm with a full bag of the pre-grated Italian Mix Cheese made by Sargento.  Then added one additional cup of mozz.  Instead of just salt, pepper and parsley, I used garlic salt, parsley, oregano, sweet basil and onion.  YUM!  The filling made enough for an entire box of manicotti noodles.  Hint:  Only pre-cook the noodles until they are slighty tender, the sauces and cheeses assist in cooking it the rest of the way.  And, to fill, try using a pastry bag!  Took me less than 5 minutes to prepare after I precooked the noodles.  A keeper.

text:
Quick tip: You don't have to pre-cook the manicotti noodles. Easier to stuff that way and saves time cooking and waiting for them to cool. They will cook in the sauce to a perfect consistency while in the oven. Just cover with tin foil and bake for 45 minutes. Remove foil and bake for an additional 15 minutes so the cheese on top melts and gets that yummy finish.

text:
This was wonderful!!  Though I did make my own sauce (I sauteed ablout 1/2 lb of mushrooms in butter and garlic and the added a 16 oz can of tomato sauce and added some basil, pepper and more garlic to taste) and I added extra mozzarella on the top toward the end of baking.  This was my first time making manicotti and the first time my husband had ever had it at all.  We both LOVED it!  and it made yummy leftovers too.  Will definatly be making again soon!  Oh and I used the zipper bag method for filling.  I left the pasta a bit more under cooked than "al dente" (the box said 7-10 minutes and I cooked them for almost 5).  WOW it was so easy!  Thanks for the recipe.

text:
Good recipe, but I needed to make modifications for the second time around.  I omitted the eggs, since they seemed to make the cheese sauce too runny.  Instead, I used 1/2 cup of Italian bread crumbs.  Also, I used 1 tablespoon of parsely and 16 ounces of mozzerella cheese. (Throw in some garlic powder too!)  Yum.  The cheese mixture was almost too easy to stuff into the pasta and came out very delicious.  Hint:  Add 1/4 of sour cream to your cheese mixture if it seems too dry before stuffing.  Enjoy!!  
  Thanks for the start of a great recipe Anny!

text:
As I make a very large pot of meat sauce and freeze several Italian meals at a time I thought I would try a Manicotti one this time.  I only followed this recipe for the filling and I did not cook the noodles like all my frozen meals with pasta in them.  simply used a piping bag to fill the hard shells adding just a bit more sauce to the bottom and the top and then freezing.  Once thawed and baked the pasta turns out perfect and not mushy.  A wonderful addition to my "mom is to busy to cook days".  Very pretty dish to serve for company too and all I had to do was pull it from the freezer.  Excellent

This recipe is a fantastic starting point, but I imagine just as it is, it would be a bit bland. I wilted some spinach and added it to the cheese mixture, as well as a couple cloves of garlic that I had minced and briefly sauteed. I also used italian seasoning instead of the parsley. I made this for a family dinner and Oh Boy! did I get fabulous compliments on this dish!  It was a fairly easy(tiny bit time consuming) to make and produced amazing flavor.  I added italian seasonings and salts to the cheese mixture and added a little more cheese(asiago, mozzarella and parmesean blend) I did use the recommendation of another and placed cheese mixture into a gallon size ziploc baggie...it helped me fill the manicotti shells so much better and it helped save  on time! A lifesaver tip for this dish, for sure! I'm making sure to keep these ingredients on hand so I can make it again soon

text:
Not bad at all. I added basil and garlic salt, but made no other changes. My husband was very happy with it. Just make sure to use good quality sauce for best results.

Edit: The second time I made this, I halved the ricotta and replaced it with more mozzarella. This made it less like meatless lasagna and more like the ooey gooey manicotti served at Italian restaurants. I also only cooked the pasta halfway before stuffing. This meant less ripped pasta and more cheese stuffed into each tube. The pasta cooked the rest of the way through in the oven and came out perfect. I added basil, garlic salt, and minced garlic to the cheese mixture as well. My dinner guests were very impressed. 

With these alterations, the recipe is definitely five stars. It tasted like restaurant quality manicotti. Three and a half stars for the original recipe, though (I rounded up).

text:
This is a great base recipe. I made it as directed and it was good.

However, I prefer more flavor, so next time I will add garlic salt and maybe some Italian sausage. I put the filling in a ziplock bag like others suggested, and it made filling the manicotti WAY easier. Also, I recommend under cooking the manicotti so that it doesn't fall apart when you fill it. It will cook all the way through when you put it in the oven.

I am a novice in the kitchen, and this recipe was extremely easy to make.  Instead of cooking the noodles ahead of time, I took the advice of someone else and placed the stuffing inside while the noodle was uncooked. I also covered the dish with foil.  With the exception of a few hard corners, the pasta came out perfect.  The sauce I used was kind of thick (e.g., couldn't pour it out of the bottle) so next time I may add a little bit of water to help steam the noodles in the cooking dish.

text:
I don't know if anyone has already made this suggestion but  I used eggroll wrappers in place of manicotti tubes. They are thinner, so you can use two for each if you want a thicker pasta (more like a manicotti shell). This way, you omit the pre-cooking of the pasta and the difficulty stuffing the tubes. Just put the cheese mixture in the wrapper(s), roll them up and place them seam-side down in the casserole dish. The wrappers cook while the dish is heating in the oven. I also add chopped fresh basil to the cheese mixture and use Rao's arabiatta sauce for spiciness. So much easier than using manicotti shells.

As suggested by others, I did not pre-cook the pasta tubes. I used the ingredients as listed, but added Italian seasoning and garlic powder, plus  about 1.5 cups of seasoned ground chicken I had on hand from another meal. country:

text:
This was such an excellent recipe.  I doubled the recipe and only used 3 eggs instead of 4, I also added 10 oz fresh spinach chopped finely, 3 links mild Italian sausage cooked and crumbled with half a sauteed onion, along with 1/2 tsp garlic powder, 1 TBS fresh Basil, 1.5 tsp dried oregano.  I mixed it all together and used a pastry bag to fill the 8oz package of Barilla manicotti noodles.  I left the noodles dry and also used a 40 oz jar of Rao's Mariniara Sauce.  I only used half of the filling so I will freeze the other half for the next manicotti meal.  I used a 10x15" glass baking dish buttered.  I added 1 cup of sauce to the bottom, then added the filled noodles, then poured the remaining marinara sauce on top, making sure to cover the noodles entirely so they would cook without having to boil them first.  This makes it so much less mess and easier to handle.  I then covered it with foil and baked it for 50 minutes, then removed the foil and baked for an additional 10 minutes. Best manicotti I have ever had!  Thank you for a great foundation recipe!

text:
This is my go to recipe for Manicotti, and it's a GREAT place to start, but I do things just a little different. 

1. I DO NOT cook my manicotti shells beforehand. Instead, I make sure to coat the bottom of my pan with a healthy layer of marinara, and then completely cover the shells with marinara and let them cook in the sauce. This maintains the integrity of the shell and lets them cook in that flavorful sauce.

2. I use some Italian seasoning in the cheese mixture, as well as garlic powder. 

3. Sometimes I also include some cooked spinach (frozen is fine), when I'm feeling a little guilty about eating just fat and carbs for dinner.

Made this with some of my dad's spaghetti sauce (he makes a big batch from scratch and then freezes it in 8- and 16-ounce containers) and it's amazing. Manicotti is  Italian for "lasagne that takes 4 times as long to make".  This recipe is good but I'll never make it again because  it's a lot easier to spread the cheese in big layers. Very good! Using only one egg worked fine for me.  Also added some garlic powder to the cheesse. I did the plastic bag, snip-off corner method to stuff the manicotti for some of them. text:
Delicous!  I love manicotti and this was an easy recipe.  Now...I will admit that I make my own pasta (which is nice and soft) AND this time I actually tried making Ina Garten's (Barefoot Contessa) homemade ricotta.  I will never buy store bought again.  OMG sooooo easy -- milk, cream...heat...add vinegar and drain through cheesecloth and voila!  In less than an hour you have 2+ cups of ricotta.   But I digress ---  threw that and other ingredients together...rolled up in a a sheet of pasta and closed with a bit of water... lined a pan with sauce and then after putting them all on top , dumped the rest of sauce on top...along with some parm and mozzarella.   Cooked for 30 minutes ...long enough to "cook" the fresh pasta and everything else really just needed some warming.  Simple meal and delicious.  If you used dried pasta, you don't have to boil it ahead, but plan on baking a good 45+ minutes to get the pasta softened!

text:
I love making this recipe!  I have made it a few times now, and definitely recommend the following adjustments: I add 1 tsp each of oregano, parsley, garlic powder, and basil.  I also usually increase the mozzarella and parmesan by about 50% and use a whole box (8oz) of manicotti.  The reviewer that recommended using a pastry bag to stuff the noodles is GENIUS!  I will never use a spoon again.  It takes about 5 minutes to stuff all the noodles with far less mess and frustration.  Also, I bake covered to avoid burning the cheese/noodles, then uncover for the last 5 minutes and add a top layer of parmesan then.  It comes out great!

text:
For the most part it's a traditional recipe but having grown up  Italian-American and having eaten my fair share of food in Italy the only change I made was cinnamon.  I mix everything EXCEPT for the eggs and then add the cinnamon and taste it until I get it just right. I would guess that for the amount of mixture I added 1/2 teaspoon of cinnamon.  Once I achieve the desired flavor I add the eggs and mix it up. I also allow the ingredients to blend for about 20 minutes before I fill the shells. Also, I used about 23-25 ounces of sauce.

Perfecto!!

Love this recipe!! I do change it up, I guess you can say "I love this recipe" when you make major changes to it, but it is an awesome manicotti base, and great as is.
